"Let's think step by step\n1. The original price of each pack of DVDs is $76.\n2. There is a discount of $25 on each pack.\n3. To find out how much you have to pay after the discount, we subtract the discount from the original price.\n4. Therefore, the amount you have to pay for each pack after the discount is $76 - $25.\n5. Performing the subtraction, we get $76 - $25 = $51.\nTherefore, you have to pay $51 for each pack of DVDs after applying a $25 discount."

"Let's think step by step\n1. Initially, there were 28 children on the bus.\n2. 82 children got on the bus.\n3. After some children got off, there were 30 children on the bus.\n4. To find out how many children got off, we subtract the initial number of children and those who got on from the final number of children on the bus.\n5. Therefore, the number of children that got off is (28 + 82) - 30 = 80.\n6. The difference between the number of children that got on and those that got off is 82 - 80 = 2.\nTherefore, 2 more children got on the bus than those that got off."
"Let's think step by step:\n1. Olivia initially had 3 dollars in her wallet.\n2. She collected 49 more dollars from an ATM.\n3. After visiting the supermarket, she had 49 dollars left.\n4. To find out how much she spent at the supermarket, we calculate her total money before shopping and subtract the amount left after shopping.\n5. Total money before shopping: 3 dollars + 49 dollars = 52 dollars.\n6. Amount spent at the supermarket: 52 dollars - 49 dollars = 3 dollars.\n7. Therefore, Olivia collected 49 dollars at the ATM and spent 3 dollars at the supermarket.\n8. To find out how much more money she collected at the ATM than she spent at the supermarket, we subtract the amount spent from the amount collected.\n9. The difference is 49 dollars - 3 dollars = 46 dollars.\n\nTherefore, Olivia collected 46 dollars more at the ATM than she spent at the supermarket."

Therefore, the number of additional games she needs to buy is 140 - 22.\n5. Performing the subtraction, we get 140 - 22 = 118.\n6. Therefore, Kelly needs to buy 118 additional Nintendo games.\nThe answer is 118"

"Let's think step by step:\n1. The initial number of children on the bus was 23.\n2. 24 children got on the bus.\n3. Let \\( x \\) be the number of children that got off the bus.\n4. The final number of children on the bus was 8.\n5. The equation representing the situation is: \\( 23 + 24 - x = 8 \\)\n6. Solving the equation, we get: \\( 47 - x = 8 \\)\n7. Rearranging the equation, we get: \\( x = 47 - 8 = 39 \\)\n8. Therefore, 39 children got off the bus.\n9. To find how many more children got off the bus than those that got on, we subtract the number of children that got on from the number that got off: \\( 39 - 24 = 15 \\)\n\nThe answer is 15."

Therefore, the number of pieces of candy in each bag is 42 divided by 2.\n5. Performing the division, we get 42 / 2 = 21.\n6. Therefore, there are 21 pieces of candy in each bag.\nThe answer is 21"
"Let's think step by step\n1. Jack received 6 emails in the morning.\n2. Jack received 2 emails in the afternoon.\n3. To find out how many more emails Jack received in the morning than in the afternoon, we subtract the number of emails in the afternoon from the number of emails in the morning.\n4. Therefore, the number of more emails Jack received in the morning than in the afternoon is 6 - 2.\n5. Performing the subtraction, we get 6 - 2 = 4.\nTherefore, Jack received 4 more emails in the morning than in the afternoon."

To find out how many more pastries than cakes he sold, we subtract the number of cakes sold from the number of pastries sold.\n4. "Let's think step by step\n1. Haley has 20 marbles.\n2. There are 2 boys in her class who love to play marbles.\n3. To find out how many marbles each boy will receive, we need to divide the total number of marbles by the number of boys.\n4. Therefore, each boy will receive 20 / 2 = 10 marbles.\n5. So, each of the 2 boys will receive 10 marbles.\nThe answer is 10."
"Let's think step by step\n1. The total number of people attending the party is 14.\n2. They currently have 4 sets of tables, with each set having 3 chairs.\n3. Therefore, the total number of chairs currently available is 4 sets * 3 chairs/set = 12 chairs.\n4. To find out how many more chairs they need to buy, we subtract the total number of chairs currently available from the total number of people attending the party.\n5. Therefore, the number of additional chairs needed is 14 - 12 = 2 chairs.\nSo, they will need to buy 2 more chairs."

To find out how much money Lewis earns during the harvest season, we first calculate his total earnings before deducting rent.\n5. Lewis earns $403 every week for 233 weeks, so his total earnings before rent is 403 * 233.\n6. Therefore, Lewis earns $403 * 233 = $93,899 during the harvest season.\n7.
